```text
Short answer: for your current hackathon scope, keep `SQLite` now and defer `Neon + Prisma` until you need hosted multi-client reliability.

1. `SQLite` vs `Neon + Prisma` for this project
- `SQLite` is faster/simpler for single-user local dev (no network hop, zero infra).
- `Neon` is better when backend is deployed and you need remote persistence, backups, team access, concurrent writers.
- Your runtime is currently wired only for SQLite; non-sqlite provider will raise (`get_store`): [database.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/database.py:316).
- You already have Prisma/Postgres schema ready, but it is not active in runtime yet: [schema.prisma](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/prisma/schema.prisma:1).

2. How it works right now (IDs, namespace, collection mapping)
- One Actian VectorDB endpoint is configured globally via host/port: [config.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/config.py:19).
- App creates one `VectorDBClient` at startup: [runtime.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/runtime.py:26).
- Control-plane DB stores metadata only (`instances`, `knowledge_bases`, `resources`, `query_logs`): [database.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/database.py:34).
- On KB create, backend generates `kb_id`, computes embedding dim, creates a VectorDB collection, and stores mapping: [knowledge_bases.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/knowledge_bases.py:29).
- Collection naming is deterministic: `kb_{instance[:8]}_{kb[:8]}`: [runtime.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/runtime.py:43).
- Ingestion uses `kb_id -> collection_name` mapping and writes payload metadata (`namespace_id`, `user_id`, etc.): [resources.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/resources.py:29), [ingestion.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/services/ingestion.py:141).
- Query/search also resolve `kb_id -> collection_name` and run vector search: [query.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/query.py:19).
- Memory flow uses a dedicated namespace (`conversation_memory`) and filters by `user_id`: [memory.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/memory.py:27), [retrieval.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/services/retrieval.py:54).
- You can inspect all current collections + KB mappings via `/collections`: [main.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/main.py:39).

3. Do we need a DB at all if not multi-user?
- Yes, even in single-user mode, you need metadata mapping:
- `kb_id -> collection_name -> embedding_model -> namespace`.
- Resource status tracking (`processing/done/failed`).
- Query logs/observability history.
- Without control-plane DB, agent integration becomes brittle (manual mapping, no lifecycle state).

4. Agent integration plan (future, practical)
- Recommended integration contract: agent talks to DocuMind HTTP APIs, not directly to Actian.
- Minimal contract for agent:
- `POST /search` and `POST /query` with `kb_id`.
- `POST /resources` for ingestion.
- Optional `POST /memory/ingest` + `POST /memory/query`.
- Next step for productization:
- Add a small `documind` CLI (`init`, `kb create`, `ingest`, `search`, `query`).
- Add an agent-tool wrapper (or MCP server) that internally calls this CLI/API.
- This gives “plug into my agent” UX without exposing raw vector DB internals.

5. Recommendation for your next phase
- Keep SQLite for now.
- Finish advanced retrieval features (filtered + hybrid fusion).
- Then add CLI wrapper for integrations.
- Move to Neon/Prisma only when deploying shared hosted backend.

If you want, I can implement a minimal `documind` CLI next so your agent can integrate in one command flow.
```

**Quick decision view**

| Resource | Simple summary | Use for your project now? |
|---|---|---|
| `all-MiniLM-L6-v2` | Fast, strong text embedding baseline (384-dim). | Yes, keep as baseline. |
| `Model2Vec` | Distills sentence-transformers into tiny static embeddings for CPU/edge. | Yes, if you need edge/on-device or very low latency. |
| `Qwen3-VL-Embedding-2B` | Multimodal embedding model (text/image/video), large (2B), 32k context. | Later, only if you truly need multimodal retrieval. |
| `Jina Embeddings v4` | Strong multimodal + multilingual retrieval model with dense/late-interaction options. | Later, powerful but heavier and more complex. |
| `EmbeddingGemma-300M` | Lightweight text embedding model for edge, multilingual, 768-dim (can truncate). | Yes, good edge alternative to test vs MiniLM. |
| `Docling` | Best immediate win for ingestion/chunking of PDFs/docs/tables/layout, with hybrid chunking support. | Yes, high priority. |
| LlamaIndex semantic chunking example | Practical adaptive chunking recipe; tune threshold based on your data. | Yes, good quick experiment path. |
| `semantic-chunkers` | Multi-modal chunking lib (text/audio/video) with multiple chunker strategies. | Maybe; promising, but less battle-tested than Docling for your current needs. |
| `all-rag-strategies` repo | Great menu of RAG patterns (rerank, query expansion, contextual retrieval, etc.). | Yes, as playbook/reference, not copy-paste production code. |

**What is most useful for you immediately**
1. Keep `MiniLM` baseline and create the 30 QA ground-truth set first.
2. Add `Docling` hybrid/context-aware chunking.
3. Add reranking (from the strategy repo ideas) before changing embedding models.
4. For edge deployment, benchmark `Model2Vec` and `EmbeddingGemma-300M` against your QA set.
5. Defer Qwen/Jina multimodal until you actually need image/video retrieval.

#### ASSISTANT 15 (`phase: final_answer`)
```text
Using `brainstorming` here to define the design before implementation.

Yes, we should build a **routing/recommendation layer**, but split it into two routers:

1. **Embedding Router (for retrieval quality)**  
2. **LLM Router (for answer generation cost/quality)**

**Recommended approach: Hybrid Router (best for your case)**  
1. Start with **rule-based routing** (fast, deterministic).  
2. Add **light intent classifier** (text vs code vs multimodal).  
3. Add **feedback loop** from observability scores to improve routing defaults.

**How it would work**

1. Ingest request comes in (`source_type`, optional `use_case`, optional override).  
2. Router picks embedding profile:  
   - `general_text_search` -> `all-MiniLM-L6-v2`  
   - `higher_quality_text` -> `all-mpnet-base-v2`  
   - `balanced_text` -> `bge-small-en-v1.5`  
   - `multimodal_text_image` -> `clip-vit-base-patch32`  
   - `code_search` -> `codebert-base`  
3. Store profile + dimension with KB/collection metadata.  
4. Query request comes in; router decides target profile/collection, embeds query with same profile, then searches.  
5. LLM router picks response model (`fast/cheap` vs `high-quality`) based on latency budget + query complexity.  
6. Observability scores (`retrieval_score`, `chunk_relevance`, `hallucination_rate`) update future routing recommendations.

**Three implementation options**

1. **Rule-based only**  
   - Pros: fastest to ship, predictable  
   - Cons: less adaptive over time

2. **Classifier-first router**  
   - Pros: smarter routing from day 1  
   - Cons: more moving parts, needs evaluation set

3. **Hybrid (recommended)**  
   - Pros: ship quickly + improve with real usage data  
   - Cons: moderate implementation complexity

**Where this plugs into your current code**

- Extend model registry in [embeddings.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/embeddings.py)  
- Add routing service (new file, e.g. `app/routing.py`)  
- Persist profile metadata in [database.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/database.py)  
- Expose profile selection in request schemas in [schemas.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/models/schemas.py)

If this direction looks right, I’ll write the router design doc and then implement **v1 rule-based hybrid skeleton** first.
```

#### ASSISTANT 21 (`phase: final_answer`)
```text
Yes, your intuition is correct. Here’s how it works in the current code.

1. `instance` ↔ `knowledge base` relation  
`knowledge_bases.instance_id` is a foreign key to `instances.id`, so one instance can have many KBs.  
See [`database.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/database.py#L58) and [`database.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/database.py#L70).

2. About your point #1 (`kb_id` generation)  
`kb_id` is generated on the server when KB is created (`uuid4`).  
See [`knowledge_bases.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/knowledge_bases.py#L53).  
Also, `/resources` does **not** return `kb_id`; it returns `resource_id` + status.  
See [`resources.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/resources.py#L96).

3. About your point #2 (why `kb_id` is required in ingest/list)  
It is required so backend knows exactly which KB/collection to write/read from.  
In ingest, backend resolves KB by `kb_id`, then uses that KB’s collection name for vector upsert.  
See [`resources.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/resources.py#L50) and [`resources.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/resources.py#L87).  
Resource rows are stored with `knowledge_base_id`, and listing is filtered by it.  
See [`database.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/database.py#L93) and [`database.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/database.py#L286).

4. About your point #3 (semantic search + anonymous user access)  
Right now, `/search` and `/query` are scoped only by `kb_id`; there is no auth/authorization layer yet.  
See [`query.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/query.py#L20).  
So today, if someone has a valid `kb_id`, they can query that KB.  
Only memory query has a `user_id` filter.  
See [`retrieval.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/services/retrieval.py#L54).

What this means practically: end users should not type `kb_id`; your frontend/backend should store it after KB creation and pass it internally. If you want, I can implement a cleaner API next where client sends `instance_id + namespace_id` and server resolves/creates KB internally so `kb_id` never appears in client requests.
```

#### ASSISTANT 27 (`phase: final_answer`)
```text
`#1` means: make `kb_id` an internal detail, not something end users must handle.

Today:
1. User creates KB.
2. API returns `kb_id`.
3. User/frontend must store and pass that `kb_id` for ingest/search/list.

Proposed UX:
1. User sends `instance_id` + `namespace_id` (or a friendly KB name/key).
2. Backend does:
- find KB for that instance+namespace
- create it if missing (optional behavior)
- use its internal `kb_id` behind the scenes
3. User never sees or passes `kb_id`.

Example request style:
```json
POST /resources
{
  "instance_id": "inst_123",
  "namespace_id": "company_docs",
  "source_type": "text",
  "content": "..."
}
```

Benefits:
- simpler client flow
- fewer ID-management bugs
- cleaner path for auth (validate instance ownership once, then resolve KB internally)

If you want, I can implement this as new “friendly” endpoints while keeping existing `kb_id` endpoints for backward compatibility.
```

#### ASSISTANT 43 (`phase: final_answer`)
```text
Yes, for your current stage this is a good design.

1. Why removing client-facing `kb_id` is good
- Better UX: clients pass business context (`instance_id + namespace_id`) instead of internal UUIDs.
- Safer API contract: `kb_id` stays internal, can change without breaking clients.
- You can still return `kb_id` in responses for debugging if needed.

2. Where `namespace_id` comes from
- It is part of KB creation input, with default `"company_docs"` in [`schemas.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/models/schemas.py#L24).
- It is stored on each KB record in [`knowledge_bases.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/knowledge_bases.py#L67).
- Runtime resolution uses `instance_id + namespace_id` via [`database.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/database.py#L233), then routers use that:
  - ingest/list: [`resources.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/resources.py#L60)
  - search/query: [`query.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/query.py#L22)

3. Practical rule for now
- Keep one namespace (`company_docs`) unless you intentionally want multiple KB buckets.
- In Postman/frontend, you can treat `namespace_id` as a stable constant.

4. One important caveat
- You should eventually enforce uniqueness of `(instance_id, namespace_id)` in DB.  
  Right now lookup uses first match, so duplicates could become ambiguous.
```

#### ASSISTANT 79 (`phase: final_answer`)
```text
Yes, we do have a few concrete doubts worth sending to the Actian developer.

You can copy-paste this as-is:

```text
Actian questions from our current backend implementation:

1) For true multimodal (text + image), should we use:
   - one shared CLIP vector space in a single vector field, or
   - named vectors (for example text_vector + image_vector)?
   What is the recommended schema in Actian for production?

2) What is the recommended ingestion pattern for images with Actian SDK?
   We currently only ingest text/markdown/pdf/url/conversation and do not yet have image binary ingestion.

3) If we use named vectors, is server-side search/fusion across multiple vector names supported directly, or should we do client-side fusion (RRF/DBSF)?

4) Is sparse-vector upsert/search fully supported in the current server version for production?
   We currently use semantic + lexical hybrid (payload keyword scoring), not sparse vectors yet.

5) For hybrid retrieval at scale, is payload scrolling + lexical scoring acceptable, or does Actian provide a better native keyword/BM25/full-text path?

6) For metadata filtering performance, should we explicitly create field indexes for fields like source_type/user_id/session_id/namespace_id?
   If yes, which field types/index strategy do you recommend?

7) For cosine distance in Actian, should embeddings be L2-normalized before upsert/query for best behavior?
   (We normalize in some model paths; want a consistent recommendation.)

8) Any recommended limits/best practices for:
   - collection count per instance
   - payload size
   - vector dimensions
   - HNSW params (m, ef_construct) by workload?

9) For query fusion, are there best-practice defaults for RRF weights and candidate limits for mixed semantic+keyword retrieval?

10) Do you recommend keeping one collection per KB namespace (our current design), or using fewer shared collections with stronger filter partitioning?
```

If you want, I can also trim this to a “top 5 only” version before you send.
```

```text
Yes, brief version:

`namespace_id` in your app is an **application-level label**, not an Actian-native namespace like Pinecone.

How association works in your code:

1. `instance_id + namespace_id` identifies a KB row in SQLite.
2. That KB row stores `collection_name`, `embedding_model`, and `embedding_dim`.
3. All chunks for that KB are written into that `collection_name` in Actian.
4. Each chunk payload also stores `kb_id`, `instance_id`, `namespace_id` for traceability/filtering.
5. Search/query first resolves KB, then searches only that collection.

So the real link is:

`instance_id + namespace_id` -> `knowledge_bases row` -> `collection_name` -> `Actian points/chunks`

Not Pinecone-style “one index + many namespaces”; your current design is “many collections (one per KB)”.

Quick flow example:
- Ingest request with `instance_id=inst1`, `namespace_id=company_docs`
- Backend resolves/creates KB
- KB has collection like `kb_abcd1234_efgh5678`
- Chunks/embeddings go into that collection
- Later `/search/instance` resolves same KB and searches same collection

Where this is implemented:
- KB -> collection naming: [runtime.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/runtime.py#L47)
- KB creation stores collection metadata: [knowledge_bases.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/knowledge_bases.py#L53)
- Instance+namespace resolve / auto-create on ingest: [resources.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/resources.py#L57)
- Chunk payload includes `kb_id/instance_id/namespace_id`: [ingestion.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/services/ingestion.py#L141)
- Query resolves KB from instance+namespace: [query.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/query.py#L32)

One caveat:
- DB uniqueness on `(instance_id, namespace_id)` is not hard-enforced yet, so ambiguous matches are possible until that constraint is added.
```

---

## The answer: Build **both**, in the right order, for the right reasons

Here's what the data actually says:

The winning strategy in 2026 is not choosing one over the other — it is using both strategically. But the key insight for DocuMind is **who your users are**.

If you are building for agents, design a good API first, then expose a simple MCP adapter on top. Let the harness do the rest. That is your exact situation — you already have the FastAPI backend from Phase 1. The MCP server is just a thin adapter layer on top of it.

---

## Why DocuMind specifically needs MCP (not just CLI)

Once the MCP server is running, any MCP-compatible client — Cursor, Claude Code, Kiro, VS Code, or a custom agent — can query your private knowledge bases using natural language with zero per-client code.

DocuMind is not a tool like `git` or `gh` that the LLM already knows from training data. It's a **custom knowledge service** — meaning CLI is only efficient for tools LLMs already know. CLI tools are 100% reliable at 1,365–8,750 tokens per task vs MCP's 32,000–82,000 tokens — but that gap exists because the model already knows CLI tools. The model doesn't know your DocuMind API, so you'd burn tokens on documentation anyway.

---

## The token cost problem with MCP — and how to solve it

Most MCP clients load every tool definition into the context window upfront. Anthropic's solution: instead of exposing tools as direct calls, present MCP servers as code-based APIs.

This is the key design decision. DocuMind's MCP server should expose **3–4 tightly scoped tools maximum**, not a giant schema dump. Each tool description must be ruthlessly short.

---

## Revised Phase 2 Plan for DocuMind

Here's how to think about it in three layers:

**Layer 1 — Keep what you have (FastAPI backend)**
Your Phase 1 `/query`, `/search`, `/memory` endpoints stay exactly as-is. Nothing changes. This is your source of truth.

**Layer 2 — Build the MCP server (the bridge)**
A thin Python MCP server that wraps your existing FastAPI endpoints as callable tools. This is what Claude Code, Cursor, Codex, and VS Code will connect to. It's maybe 150 lines of code using `fastmcp`.

Expose exactly **4 tools** — no more:
- `search_docs(query, kb_id, top_k?)` — semantic search, returns raw chunks + scores
- `ask_docs(question, kb_id)` — full RAG answer with citations via your agent endpoint
- `ingest_text(content, kb_id, source_ref?)` — add text/markdown to a KB on the fly
- `list_knowledge_bases(instance_id?)` — discover available KBs

**Layer 3 — Build the CLI (for developer workflows)**
A `documind` CLI that wraps the same FastAPI backend. This is for terminal users, CI pipelines, and scripting. It's also what makes DocuMind composable with other Unix tools (`documind search "deploy process" | grep payments`).

---

## Concrete implementation

**MCP server** (`mcp_server/server.py`):

```python
from fastmcp import FastMCP
import httpx
import os

BASE_URL = os.getenv("DOCUMIND_API_URL", "http://localhost:8000")
mcp = FastMCP("DocuMind", instructions=(
    "Search and query private enterprise documentation. "
    "Use search_docs for quick lookup. Use ask_docs for full answers with citations."
))

@mcp.tool()
def search_docs(query: str, kb_id: str, top_k: int = 5) -> str:
    """Search a knowledge base semantically. Returns relevant chunks with source citations."""
    r = httpx.post(f"{BASE_URL}/search", json={"kb_id": kb_id, "query": query, "top_k": top_k})
    results = r.json().get("results", [])
    if not results:
        return "No relevant documentation found."
    return "\n\n---\n".join(
        f"[{i+1}] {res['source_ref']} (score: {res['score']:.2f})\n{res['text']}"
        for i, res in enumerate(results)
    )

@mcp.tool()
def ask_docs(question: str, kb_id: str) -> str:
    """Ask a question and get a full grounded answer with source citations."""
    r = httpx.post(f"{BASE_URL}/query", json={"kb_id": kb_id, "question": question}, timeout=30)
    data = r.json()
    answer = data.get("answer", "No answer generated.")
    sources = data.get("sources", [])
    if sources:
        citations = "\n".join(f"  - {s['source_ref']} (score: {s['score']:.2f})" for s in sources)
        return f"{answer}\n\nSources:\n{citations}"
    return answer

@mcp.tool()
def ingest_text(content: str, kb_id: str, source_ref: str = "inline") -> str:
    """Add text or markdown content to a knowledge base."""
    r = httpx.post(f"{BASE_URL}/resources", data={
        "kb_id": kb_id, "source_type": "text",
        "content": content, "source_ref": source_ref
    })
    data = r.json()
    return f"Indexed {data.get('chunks_indexed', 0)} chunks from '{source_ref}'."

@mcp.tool()
def list_knowledge_bases(instance_id: str = "") -> str:
    """List available knowledge bases. Optionally filter by instance_id."""
    r = httpx.get(f"{BASE_URL}/knowledge-bases")
    kbs = r.json()
    if not kbs:
        return "No knowledge bases found."
    return "\n".join(f"- {kb['name']} (id: {kb['id']}, namespace: {kb['namespaceId']})" for kb in kbs)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    mcp.run()
```

**Config snippet users drop into their agent** (`mcp.json`):
```json
{
  "mcpServers": {
    "documind": {
      "command": "uv",
      "args": ["run", "python", "mcp_server/server.py"],
      "env": {
        "DOCUMIND_API_URL": "http://localhost:8000"
      }
    }
  }
}
```

This works in **Claude Code**, **Cursor**, **Windsurf**, and **VS Code** with zero changes. Users just point `DOCUMIND_API_URL` at wherever DocuMind is running.

**CLI** (`cli/documind.py`) — build this after MCP:
```bash
documind search "how do I deploy payments?" --kb eng-docs
documind ask "what is our auth flow?" --kb eng-docs
documind ingest README.md --kb eng-docs
documind kbs list
```

---

## Updated Phase 2 sequence

1. Install `fastmcp` — `pip install fastmcp`
2. Build the 4-tool MCP server wrapping your existing API (≈150 lines)
3. Test it locally in Claude Code with a real KB
4. Add the `CLAUDE.md` / `AGENTS.md` skill file that tells agents when and how to use each tool
5. Build the CLI as a thin Click/Typer wrapper over the same API
6. Ship both together — MCP for IDE/agent harness users, CLI for terminal/CI users

The LangChain agent you already have in Phase 1 stays exactly where it is — it's the engine that runs when `ask_docs` is called. The MCP server is just the door that lets external agents in.

"# Phase 2 Robustness Questions (MCP + CLI)

Date: 2026-04-15

## 1) Product Scope and Success

1. Is Phase 2 success defined as "works in one MCP client" or "works consistently across Claude Code + Cursor + VS Code"? 
> Yes, we are optimizing more towards AI agents and harnesses such as Open Code Codex and Claude Code. These are the agent CLI things, AI agent sort of things, and we need to have work consistently across everything. 
Eventually, we are focusing more on Claude Code-cli, codex-cli, and opencode which are  AI-powered terminal agents 

2. What is the minimum acceptable quality bar for `ask_docs` output (citation presence, answer accuracy, fallback behavior)?
> So an AI agent can eventually have some sort of tools, and they can just use those tools. After using that tool, there might be some sort of chances that the AI agent asks in a different way and did not get the answer, so for another try and fallback, it will be asking another time using another question. That specific thing could be used, and if he got the response, then okay. If he did not get the response, he will just move forward with whatever context it has, because there might be chances that the question that the AI agent is asking is not available in the documentation. We need to be not super bullish on getting the answer; we need to be bullish on getting fast responses. 

3. Which workflow is most critical on day one: search, ask, ingest, or KB discovery?
> I don't think any of this is super critical because we will be building tools that will be exposed as CLI, and every tool will be working super fine. > out of scope:
- auth
- admin UI
- multi-hop tools
- async pipelines (keep sync first)

(it maybe required for MCP server)
from actian_vectorai import AsyncVectorAIClient, VectorParams, Distance, PointStruct

async def main():
    async with AsyncVectorAIClient("localhost:50051") as client:
        await client.collections.create(
            "demo",
            vectors_config=VectorParams(size=128, distance=Distance.Cosine),
        )
        await client.points.upsert("demo", [
            PointStruct(id=1, vector=[0.1] * 128, payload={"tag": "hello"}),
        ])
        results = await client.points.search("demo", vector=[0.1] * 128, limit=5)
        print(results)
        await client.collections.delete("demo")

asyncio.run(main())

## 2) API Contract Decisions

1. Should MCP tools use `kb_id` only, or move to `instance_id + namespace_id` to match current preferred backend contract?
> MCP tool will be using instance ID plus namespace ID because that is something that we have been exposed to and are using it. If KB ID will be more efficient internally for MCP tool, maybe we'll use that. Whatever feels well, we will go with that. 

2. Will `search_docs` map to `/search` or `/search/advanced` by default? 
> yes, and advanced search will be only used when we did not get the search for that specific keyword, so we will be using advanced search because it takes time and latency. What if we did not get a response at the first advanced search? We will just move on. 

3. Will `ask_docs` map to `/query` or `/query/advanced` by default?
> yes, and advance only be used when we get response at the first place. 

4. Do we freeze response schemas now (for MCP + CLI stability) and version them if changed later? (can you explain this more) ***

## 3) MCP Tool Surface (Keep It Small, Stable)

1. Are the first 4 tools final (`search_docs`, `ask_docs`, `ingest_text`, `list_knowledge_bases`)?
> yes 
2. Should each tool have strict parameter limits (e.g., `top_k <= 20`, content size caps)?
> yes 
3. What is the standard tool error shape (not-found, validation, timeout, server error)?
> server errro | not-found (what ever is the good user experice)

4. Should tools return plain text, structured JSON, or both (for client compatibility)?
> Tools should return structured JSON as the primary response format, 
but also support an optional human-readable representation.
Reasoning:
- AI agents and MCP-compatible clients require structured outputs for reliable parsing, chaining, and decision-making.
- JSON ensures schema consistency, forward compatibility, and easier validation.
- However, some clients (CLI, debugging, logs, fallback UX) benefit from readable text.

Decision:
- Primary: structured JSON (strict schema)
- Optional: derived text field (for display only, not parsing)

Example:
{
  "status": "success",
  "data": {...},
  "meta": {...},
  "text": "Human-readable summary (optional)"
} 

## 4) Safety and Tenant Isolation

1. Can one MCP server instance access multiple tenants, and if yes, how do we prevent cross-tenant leakage?
>YES multi-tenant allowed
enforce:
instance_id + namespace_id required on every call

2. Is there a required allowlist for target KBs per client/user session?(can you explin this more) *** [dont make it complex we are in hackathon not prodcution]
"

#### ASSISTANT 61 (`phase: final_answer`)
```text
You’re right, and your diagnosis is correct: this was mostly backend/tool-choice latency, not just “MCP is slow”.

**What caused the 30–35s behavior**
1. `ask_docs` does full `/query` flow (retrieval + answer generation), which is heavier than `search_docs`.
2. Agent did `ask_docs` first, got weak/unknown output, then did `search_docs` again, so time stacked.
3. MCP overhead exists, but usually small; the heavy part is backend query + LLM path.

**Who is pinging (`too_many_pings`)**
- It is the backend’s Actian gRPC client (VectorAI), not Codex directly.
- Your log shows default keepalive at `30000ms`; server throttled it with `ENHANCE_YOUR_CALM`.

I applied fixes now.

### Changes made
- Faster ask behavior for MCP tool calls (force fast profile + latency-sensitive):
  - [service.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/mcp_server/service.py:191)
- Stronger MCP guidance to use `search_docs` first for exact/factual lookups:
  - [server.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/mcp_server/server.py:24)
- OpenAI timeout guard (so query path fails fast instead of hanging long):
  - [config.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/config.py:34)
  - [agent.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/services/agent.py:46)
- gRPC keepalive tuning to reduce ping spam:
  - [vectordb.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/vectordb.py:21)
  - env knobs documented in [.env.example](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/.env.example:4)

  - `python -m unittest discover -s tests -v`
- Result: all tests passed (`37` total).

---

### CLI vs MCP (your Q3)
Yes: **CLI-first is a good strategy** for your hackathon.
- CLI is typically faster and more deterministic for agent terminal workflows.
- MCP is still useful as compatibility layer for clients that need MCP.
- Important: CLI won’t remove backend/LLM latency; it mainly removes MCP orchestration overhead.

If you want, next I’ll start `P2-T6` immediately as CLI-first (`documind search-docs / ask-docs / ingest-text / list-kbs`) and keep MCP as fallback path.
```

#### ASSISTANT 70 (`phase: final_answer`)
```text
You’re pointing at the right UX gap.

**Current behavior (today)**
- Query/search needs `instance_id + namespace_id`; if KB doesn’t exist, backend returns 404 ([query.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/query.py:32)).
- MCP tools also require both fields ([service.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/mcp_server/service.py:76)).
- Ingest can auto-create a KB for an existing instance+namespace, but not a missing instance ([resources.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/resources.py:59)).

**What we should do for good UX (hackathon-friendly)**
1. Add a one-time setup: `documind init`.
2. In `init`: create/select instance, choose namespace (default `company_docs`), save as local default context.
3. For all CLI calls: if `--instance-id/--namespace-id` not passed, auto-use saved context.
4. If no context exists: interactive prompt (CLI) instead of hard failure.
5. If namespace/KB missing: return structured error with suggestions (`available_namespaces`, `next_steps`).
6. If no docs indexed yet: return “empty KB” guidance with the exact `ingest-text` command to run.
7. Never auto-search across instances; optional fallback can search other namespaces **within same instance** only if explicitly enabled.

This gives new users a smooth start without asking instance/namespace every time, while keeping tenant isolation clear.

If you want, I can implement this as `P2-T7` now:
- `documind init`
- local context file
- auto-context resolution in CLI
- better error/suggestion payloads for MCP and CLI.
```

#### ASSISTANT 71 (`phase: final_answer`)
```text
Your direction is correct.  
For this UX, treat `instance_id + namespace_id` as an **active context** that can be persisted and switched.

**Refined design**

1. Add persistent active context  
- Store `context_id -> instance_id, namespace_id, updated_at` in SQLite (same backend DB).  
- `context_id` comes from env (`DOCUMIND_CONTEXT_ID`) for MCP; CLI uses `default` unless overridden.

2. Add context tools (MCP + CLI parity)  
- `get_active_context()`  
- `set_active_context(instance_id, namespace_id)`  
- `list_instances()`  
- `list_namespaces(instance_id)` (derived from KBs for that instance)

3. Make existing tools context-aware  
- `search_docs`, `ask_docs`, `ingest_text` accept optional `instance_id`, `namespace_id`.  
- If missing, resolve from active context.  
- If no active context, return structured action-required payload:
```json
{
  "status":"error",
  "meta":{"error":"validation_error","reason":"context_missing"},
  "data":{"action_required":"set_active_context"}
}
```
- This keeps your current error enum stable.

4. First-time user flow  
- User asks question with no context.  
- Tool returns `context_missing` + available instances/namespaces hints.  
- Agent asks user once, then calls `set_active_context`.  
- Next calls reuse it automatically.

5. “Switch instance/namespace” flow  
- User says “switch to instance X”.  
- Agent calls `list_namespaces(instance_id=X)`, asks user to pick.  
- Agent calls `set_active_context(X, chosen_namespace)`.  
- All later calls use new context unless explicitly overridden.

6. No-instance/no-KB case  
- If no instances exist, return action-required: `create_instance`.  
- After first ingest, KB auto-creates for chosen namespace (already supported in `/resources`).

7. Docs updates needed  
- MCP instructions: “If context missing, ask user to select instance+namespace and call `set_active_context` before query tools.”  
- CLI docs: add `documind init`, `documind context show/set`.

If you approve this exact contract, I can implement it next as `P2-T7` with minimal hackathon-safe scope.
```

9) Provide final summary:
   - pages crawled
   - pages ingested
   - failures
   - sample source_refs
10) After successful validation, use retrieved docs as primary reference to implement features.

If docs are insufficient, say exactly what is missing and continue with best effort.

#### ASSISTANT 129 (`phase: final_answer`)
```text
You’re correct. This run shows **orchestration drift**, not just answer-quality issues.

Where it went wrong:

1. **Wrong execution path**
- Log shows MCP calls (`Called documind.*`), not `dcli`.
- So your DCLI skill policy was not actually controlling behavior in that session.

2. **Cross-project context leak**
- It used `context_id: "default"` (shared), so it started from unrelated context.
- That explains why it saw old instance/namespace first.

3. **No hard guard before creating context**
- MCP exposes `create_instance` directly and model can call it without user confirmation ([server.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/mcp_server/server.py:99)).
- `set_active_context` accepts unknown namespace and still persists it (`namespace_known` can be false) ([service.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/mcp_server/service.py:194), [service.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/mcp_server/service.py:211)).

4. **Ingest quality was too thin**
- It ingested only a few summarized notes (1 chunk each), not full docs.
- Then `ask_docs` is intentionally strict and may return “I don’t know” if evidence is insufficient ([agent.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/services/agent.py:56)).

5. **Side-channel doc reading**
- It read `.documind/svelte_docs` files directly, bypassing normal retrieval discipline.

So yes, this behavior is possible with current MCP surface unless guarded.

What to fix (priority):

1. Set per-project MCP context in config:
- `DOCUMIND_CONTEXT_ID=<repo_slug>` (never `default` for multi-project use)

2. Enforce policy in agent prompt:
- “Do not call `create_instance` or `set_active_context` without asking user first.”

3. Add server-side hard guard (best fix):
- Require explicit confirmation for `create_instance`
- Reject `set_active_context` to unknown namespace unless explicit override flag

If you want, I can implement #3 now so this is blocked by backend rules (not just prompt behavior).
```

#### ASSISTANT 132 (`phase: final_answer`)
```text
You were right. The issue was on the MCP path, not DCLI.

I added hard guards in MCP server so this can’t auto-drift as before:

1. `create_instance` now requires explicit confirmation
- New MCP arg: `confirm_create=true`
- Without it, it returns validation error (`confirmation_required`)

2. `set_active_context` now blocks unknown namespaces by default
- New MCP arg: `allow_unknown_namespace=true` (override only)
- Without override, if namespace is not known for that instance, it returns validation error (`namespace_unknown`) and includes `available_namespaces`

Changed files:
- [server.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/mcp_server/server.py)

#### ASSISTANT 133 (`phase: final_answer`)
```text
Yes. From your log, the fallback to MCP is expected for 3 reasons:

1. **DCLI retrieval failed first**
- You got `status: "error"` / `"search request failed."` and `"ask request failed."`
- Once CLI path fails, Codex often tries the next available tool path (your MCP server).

2. **`context-id` mismatch**
- You set context with `--context-id demo-test-app`, then searched without `--context-id`.
- That means later calls defaulted to `context_id=default`, not your project context.

3. **CLI backend env likely not aligned**
- `DOCUMIND_API_URL` was `<unset>`.
- CLI then relies on default `http://localhost:8000`; if that endpoint is not reachable in that session, DCLI fails and agent switches to MCP.

Also, MCP is still enabled in that Codex session, so fallback is possible by design.

### Quick fix checklist
Use this exact flow:

```bash
export DOCUMIND_API_URL="http://localhost:8000"
CID="demo-test-app"

dcli --context-id "$CID" context-show --bot=true
dcli --context-id "$CID" search-docs --qr "Svelte state management" --top-k 5 --bot=true
dcli --context-id "$CID" ask-docs -qs "In Svelte 5, shared state best practice?" --top-k 5 --bot=true
```

And verify backend reachability:

```bash
curl -sS "${DOCUMIND_API_URL}/instances" | head
```

### To stop this behavior permanently
Add this hard rule in your Codex prompt/skill:

- “If any `dcli` command returns `status=error`, **stop and ask user**. Do **not** call `documind.*` MCP tools as fallback.”

If you want, I can patch your `SKILL.md` with this exact no-fallback rule now.
```

#### ASSISTANT 134 (`phase: commentary`)
```text
I’m patching the universal `SKILL.md` now with a strict “no MCP fallback if DCLI fails” policy, so agents stop and ask instead of switching toolchains.
```

- [SKILL.md](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/docs/codex-skills/dcli/SKILL.md)

- `Failure Handling (Strict)`
- If any `dcli` call returns `status="error"`, agent must stop, show error, ask user.
- Explicitly forbids silent fallback to MCP `documind.*`.
- Forbids automatic toolchain switching and implicit instance/namespace creation on error.
- Allows only explicit DCLI context-repair steps.

What happened in simple terms:

1. Agent tried `dcli` first.

So this is mostly **fallback behavior after DCLI failure**, not random behavior.

### Most likely causes from your log
- `DOCUMIND_API_URL` was unset.
- You set context with `--context-id demo-test-app`, but later retrieval calls missed `--context-id`.
- Skill likely not reloaded in Codex (stale copy), so strict “don’t fallback to MCP” rule may not have been active.

Recommended approach:
1. Create a docs-only app at `/documentation` (static-first, no backend dependency).
2. Host only that docs app (Cloudflare Pages/Vercel).
3. Treat it as “product + architecture + usage” documentation, not live SaaS.

Docs structure I’d use:
1. `What is DocuMind` (problem, value, scope).
2. `How it works` (ingest → chunk → embed → retrieve → answer).
3. `Architecture` (your diagram + component explanations).
4. `Components` (FastAPI API, retrieval, observability, frontend dashboard).
5. `DCLI` (quick start + command table).
6. `DocuMind MCP Server` (tools, context model, guardrails).
7. `Demo Runbook` (how judges can run locally).
8. `Current limits + roadmap` (very important for credibility).

Short definitions for docs:
- `DCLI`: terminal interface for humans/agents to run DocuMind operations.
- `DocuMind MCP Server`: MCP tool layer exposing DocuMind capabilities to AI clients.
- `Document MCP server`: same concept; use one consistent name in docs (`DocuMind MCP Server`).

## Architecture at a Glance

```
API Routes (app/api/)          → NextResponse envelopes { data, error }
        ↕
lib/api-client.ts              → Thin fetch wrapper, auto-unwraps envelopes
        ↕
lib/types/                     → Shared input/output type contracts
        ↕
hooks/queries.ts               → All read operations (useQuery)
hooks/mutations.ts             → All write operations (useMutation)
        ↕
Components / Pages             → Consume hooks, never call fetch directly
```

---

## 1. API Envelope — Single Contract for Every Response

Every API route returns a uniform `ApiEnvelope<T>`:

```ts
type ApiEnvelope<T> = {
  data: T | null
  error: { code: ApiErrorCode; message: string } | null
}
```

**Success:** `{ data: <payload>, error: null }` — returned via `ok(data)`.  
**Failure:** `{ data: null, error: { code, message } }` — returned via `fail(code, message, status)`.

This means the client never has to guess the response shape. One envelope, everywhere.

---

## 2. API Client — Fetch Wrapper That Unwraps for You

`lib/api-client.ts` exports a single `api` instance:

```ts
export const api = createApiClient({ baseURL: '/api' })
```

The client:

- Auto-serializes JSON bodies and sets `Content-Type`.
- Auto-unwraps `ApiEnvelope` → returns `data` directly or throws `ApiClientError` with the envelope's error.
- Supports timeout, abort signals, and query params out of the box.
- Exposes `get`, `post`, `patch`, `put`, `delete` — mirrors REST semantics exactly.

**What this means for hooks:** Every `api.get(...)` or `api.post(...)` call returns the **unwrapped data type** directly, not the envelope. Errors surface as thrown `ApiClientError` instances with `.code`, `.status`, and `.message`.

---

## 3. Type Contracts — `lib/types/`

Each domain has its own file (`gallery.ts`, `shared-resource.ts`, etc.) containing:

- **Input types** — what the client sends (`CreateGalleryInput`, `PresignUploadInput`)
- **Output types** — what the server returns (`GalleryListItem`, `GalleryDetail`)

These types are imported by **both** the hooks and the API routes, acting as the shared contract between client and server. No `any`, no guessing.

```
lib/types/
  gallery.ts           → GalleryListItem, GalleryDetail, CreateGalleryInput, etc.
  shared-resource.ts   → SharedResourceListItem, PublicSharedResource, etc.
  agent-api-key.ts     → AgentApiKey types
```

---

## 4. Query Hooks — `hooks/queries.ts`

### Query Key Factory

A single `queryKeys` object defines every cache key in one place:

```ts
export const queryKeys = {
  galleries: ()              => ['galleries'] as const,
  gallery: (id: string)      => ['galleries', id] as const,
  sharedResources: ()        => ['shared-resources'] as const,
  sharedResource: (id: string) => ['shared-resources', id] as const,
  // ...
}
```

**Why:** Cache invalidation in mutations references these same keys — no magic strings scattered across files.

### Hook Shape

Each query hook is a thin, single-purpose function:

```ts
export function useGalleries() {
  return useQuery({
    queryKey: queryKeys.galleries(),
    queryFn: () => api.get('/galleries') as Promise<GalleryListItem[]>,
    ...realtimeQueryOptions,
  })
}
```

Rules:
- **One hook per endpoint.** No multi-purpose "useFetch" abstractions.
- **Typed return.** The `as Promise<T>` cast matches the API contract from `lib/types/`.
- **`enabled` guard** when the query depends on a parameter: `enabled: Boolean(id)`.
- **Shared options** (`realtimeQueryOptions`) keep refetch behavior consistent without repeating config.

---

## 5. Mutation Hooks — `hooks/mutations.ts`

### Hook Shape

```ts
export function useCreateGallery() {
  const queryClient = useQueryClient()

  return useMutation({
    mutationFn: (body: CreateGalleryInput) =>
      api.post('/galleries', body) as Promise<GalleryListItem>,
    onSuccess: async () => {
      await invalidateGalleryData(queryClient)
    },
  })
}
```

Rules:
- **One hook per action.** `useCreateGallery`, `useDeleteGallery`, `useRevokeSharedResource`, etc.
- **Input is typed.** The `mutationFn` parameter matches the input type from `lib/types/`.
- **Cache invalidation lives in `onSuccess`.** The component doesn't touch the query cache — ever.
- **Invalidation helpers** (`invalidateGalleryData`, `invalidateShareData`) group related cache busts and run them in parallel.

### Invalidation Helpers

```ts
async function invalidateGalleryData(queryClient, galleryId?: string) {
  const tasks: Promise<unknown>[] = []
  tasks.push(
    queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: queryKeys.galleries() }),
    queryClient.refetchQueries({ queryKey: queryKeys.galleries() }),
  )
  if (galleryId) {
    tasks.push(
      queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: queryKeys.gallery(galleryId) }),
      queryClient.refetchQueries({ queryKey: queryKeys.gallery(galleryId) }),
    )
  }
  await Promise.all(tasks)
}
```

This keeps cache logic DRY — multiple mutations that affect galleries share the same invalidation path.

---

## 6. Component Consumption — The Rules

### Queries

```tsx
const galleriesQuery = useGalleries()
const sharedResourcesQuery = useSharedResources()
```

- Access data via `query.data`, fallback with `?? []`.
- Show skeletons with `query.isPending`.
- Show error state with `query.isError` + `query.error?.message`.
- Offer retry via `query.refetch()`.
- Derive computed state with `useMemo` over `query.data`.

### Mutations

```tsx
const deleteGallery = useDeleteGallery()
```

- **Always use `mutateAsync`** inside async handlers with `try/catch`:

```tsx
const handleDelete = async (id: string) => {
  try {
    await deleteGallery.mutateAsync(id)
    toast.success('Gallery deleted')
  } catch (error) {
    toast.error(error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to delete gallery')
  }
}
```

- Disable buttons with `mutation.isPending`.
- Show spinners with `mutation.isPending`.
- **Never call `api.post(...)` directly in a component.** Always go through a mutation hook.

---

## 7. The Layered Responsibility

| Layer | Responsibility | Does NOT do |
|---|---|---|
| **API Route** | Validate, query DB, return `ApiEnvelope` | Touch React, manage cache |
| **API Client** | Serialize, fetch, unwrap envelope, throw errors | Know about React or TanStack Query |
| **Type Contracts** | Define shapes for inputs and outputs | Contain logic |
| **Query Hooks** | Declare cache keys, fetch via `api.get` | Mutate data, manage UI state |
| **Mutation Hooks** | Write via `api.post/patch/delete`, invalidate cache | Manage UI state, show toasts |
| **Components** | Call hooks, handle loading/error/success UI | Call `fetch`, touch cache directly |

---

## 8. Checklist for Adding a New Feature

1. **Define types** in `lib/types/<domain>.ts` — inputs and outputs.
2. **Build the API route** in `app/api/<domain>/` — use `ok()` and `fail()` helpers.
3. **Add query key** to `queryKeys` in `hooks/queries.ts`.
4. **Add query hook** if it's a read operation.
5. **Add mutation hook** if it's a write operation — include `onSuccess` cache invalidation.
6. **Consume in component** — use the hook, handle `isPending`/`isError`, show toasts on mutation results.

No step touches another layer's concern. That's the whole point.

---

## 9. Anti-Patterns to Avoid

| Don't | Do Instead |
|---|---|
| `fetch('/api/...')` in a component | Use a query or mutation hook |
| Inline cache invalidation in components | Put it in the mutation hook's `onSuccess` |
| Magic string query keys like `['galleries']` | Use `queryKeys.galleries()` |
| `any` on API responses | Type the return with shared contracts from `lib/types/` |
| Giant multi-purpose hooks | One hook per endpoint/action |
| Swallowing errors silently | `try/catch` + `toast.error(error.message)` |
| Duplicating invalidation logic | Use shared helpers like `invalidateGalleryData` |
"
```

#### USER 7
```text
forget about the standard i have given you 

i have added the integration startdard.md check that update the todos and dont make so big todo, devide it into 4 phase and we are done
```

```text

```

#### USER 12
```text
can you fix this pelase
"## Error Type
Console Error

## Error Message
A tree hydrated but some attributes of the server rendered HTML didn't match the client properties. This won't be patched up. This can happen if a SSR-ed Client Component used:

- A server/client branch `if (typeof window !== 'undefined')`.
- Variable input such as `Date.now()` or `Math.random()` which changes each time it's called.
- Date formatting in a user's locale which doesn't match the server.
- External changing data without sending a snapshot of it along with the HTML.
- Invalid HTML tag nesting.

It can also happen if the client has a browser extension installed which messes with the HTML before React loaded.

https://react.dev/link/hydration-mismatch

  ...

      <AppDevOverlayErrorBoundary globalError={[...]}>

          <HTTPAccessFallbackBoundary notFound={<NotAllowedRootHTTPFallbackError>}>
            <HTTPAccessFallbackErrorBoundary pathname="/" notFound={<NotAllowedRootHTTPFallbackError>} ...>
              <RedirectBoundary>
                <RedirectErrorBoundary router={{...}}>
                  <Head>
                  <__next_root_layout_boundary__>
                    <SegmentViewNode type="layout" pagePath="layout.tsx">
                      <SegmentTrieNode>
                      <link>
                      <script>
                      <script>

```text
I’m using the `writing-plans` skill to create the implementation plan.

# TanStack Router + Skeleton Loading Integration Plan

**Goal:** Migrate the frontend from Next App Router navigation to TanStack Router with route-level data loading and consistent skeleton UX, while keeping current API integration (`@tanstack/react-query`) and existing styled UI.

**Recommended migration mode (fast + safe):**  
Incremental cutover in the same repo with a router shell first, then page-by-page route migration, then removal of old Next route files.

## 1. Architecture Decision (Day 0)
1. Use **TanStack Router + TanStack Query** as the app navigation/data runtime.
2. Keep Next only as host during migration, then cut over fully.
3. Use **code-based routes** first (faster to ship than file-codegen in this setup).

## 2. Target File Structure
Create:
- `documind/frontend/router/index.tsx`
- `documind/frontend/router/routeTree.tsx`
- `documind/frontend/router/root-route.tsx`
- `documind/frontend/router/routes/*.tsx` (overview, instances, kbs, resources, search, ask, chat, system)
- `documind/frontend/lib/query-keys.ts`
- `documind/frontend/lib/router-paths.ts`
- `documind/frontend/components/navigation/app-link.tsx`
- `documind/frontend/components/navigation/use-app-navigate.ts`
- `documind/frontend/components/skeletons/*.tsx` (page + panel skeletons)
- `documind/frontend/components/errors/route-error.tsx`

Modify:
- `documind/frontend/app/layout.tsx`
- `documind/frontend/app/(dashboard)/layout.tsx`
- `documind/frontend/components/app-sidebar.tsx`
- `documind/frontend/components/top-bar.tsx`
- `documind/frontend/components/command-palette.tsx`
- `documind/frontend/lib/api.ts`
- `documind/frontend/lib/query-provider.tsx`

## 3. Implementation Phases

### Phase 1: Router Core + Host Wiring
1. Install router deps (`@tanstack/react-router`, `@tanstack/router-devtools` optional).
2. Build `router/index.tsx` with `createRouter`.
3. Wire `RouterProvider` into dashboard shell in `app/(dashboard)/layout.tsx`.
4. Keep old pages temporarily to avoid hard break.

### Phase 2: Query Key Normalization + Loader Contracts
1. Add `lib/query-keys.ts` for all query keys.
2. For each route, define loader using `queryClient.ensureQueryData`.
3. Add typed search params validation for list/filter routes.

### Phase 3: Navigation Adapter Layer
1. Replace `next/link` and `next/navigation` usage in sidebar/top bar/command palette with router adapters.
2. Add `AppLink` and `useAppNavigate` wrappers for consistent usage.
3. Add route preloading on sidebar hover/focus.

### Phase 4: Skeleton System (Global + Per Route)
1. Create reusable skeleton primitives:
- table rows
- cards
- form panels
- sidebars/sheets
2. Add route `pendingComponent` per page.
3. Use panel-level skeletons for partial loads (ex: results pane loading but filters interactive).
4. Keep background refetch subtle (no full-page flash on `isFetching`).

### Phase 5: Route-by-Route Migration Order
1. Overview
2. Instances
3. Knowledge Bases
4. Resources
5. Search
6. Ask
7. Chat
8. System

For each route:
1. Move existing page component into `router/routes/*`.
2. Add loader + pending + error boundary.
3. Validate navigation, filters, dialogs, deep links.
4. Remove old Next page only after parity passes.

### Phase 6: API Efficiency Hardening
1. Add `AbortSignal` support to `lib/api.ts` requests.
2. Prevent stale race updates on fast route switches.
3. Ensure form upload keeps correct `FormData` behavior.
4. Standardize error shape consumption in route error components.

### Phase 7: Performance + UX
1. Route-level lazy loading (`lazyRouteComponent` pattern).
2. Preload likely-next routes from sidebar/command palette.
3. Tune query defaults by data type:
- static-ish metadata: longer `staleTime`
- high-churn data: short `staleTime`
4. Keep perceived responsiveness with optimistic local UI only for low-risk mutations (create instance/kb).

### Phase 8: Verification + Cutover
1. Full build and runtime smoke.
2. Manual flows against running backend:
- create instance/kb/resource
- search/ask/chat responses
- system page health/collections
3. Remove old Next route files post parity.
4. Final cleanup of obsolete imports and route utilities.

## 4. Skeleton Loading Standards (enforced)
1. First load: full structured skeleton matching final layout.
2. Filter/search transitions: keep shell mounted, skeleton only data region.
3. Mutation in progress: button-level spinner only.
4. Sticky side panels: independent skeleton lifecycle.
5. No layout shift: skeleton dimensions match real rows/cards exactly.

## 5. Efficiency Guardrails
1. Don’t rewrite business logic while migrating routes.
2. Migrate pages with minimal render diff first.
3. Centralize query keys before route migration.
4. Keep adapters for nav to avoid touching every component twice.
5. Use one “parity checklist” per route before deleting legacy page.

## 6. Fast Execution Timeline
1. Day 1: Router core + adapters + query key layer + first 2 routes.
2. Day 2: Remaining routes + skeleton pass.
3. Day 3: API abort optimization + full QA + cleanup/cutover.

## Questions Before Execution
1. Do you want **incremental cutover** (recommended) or **big-bang migration** in one PR?
2. Should we keep Next as host long-term, or fully remove Next route dependency after migration?
3. For mutations, do you want optimistic UI everywhere, or only for create actions (safer)?
```

```text
Yes, currently it’s true in your local setup.

I checked and found:

- `documind/frontend/.env` has `NEXT_PUBLIC_API_URL=http://localhost:8000`
- `curl http://localhost:8000/instances` returns `000` (connection failed)
- `curl http://localhost:8000/health` also returns `000`
- No process is listening on port `8000` (`lsof -iTCP:8000` is empty)

So the frontend is pointing to backend on `:8000`, but backend is not running.

Run backend:

```bash
cd documind/backend
source .venv/bin/activate
uvicorn app.main:app --reload --port 8000
```

Then verify quickly:

```bash
curl http://localhost:8000/health
curl http://localhost:8000/instances
```

I also created your local testing/handoff file here:

here is the script
"#!/usr/bin/env python3
from __future__ import annotations

import argparse
import json
import re
import time
from collections import deque
from dataclasses import dataclass
from datetime import datetime, timezone
from html import unescape
from html.parser import HTMLParser
from pathlib import Path
from urllib.parse import urljoin, urlparse, urlunparse
from urllib.request import Request, urlopen

ALLOWED_HOSTS = {"svelte.dev", "www.svelte.dev"}
ALLOWED_PREFIX = "/docs/svelte/"

def normalize_url(raw: str, base_url: str | None = None) -> str | None:
    joined = urljoin(base_url or "", raw)
    parsed = urlparse(joined)
    if parsed.scheme not in {"http", "https"}:
        return None
    if parsed.netloc not in ALLOWED_HOSTS:
        return None
    path = parsed.path or "/"
    if not path.startswith(ALLOWED_PREFIX):
        return None
    normalized_path = path.rstrip("/") or "/"
    return urlunparse(("https", "svelte.dev", normalized_path, "", "", ""))

def fetch_html(url: str, timeout_seconds: int) -> str:
    request = Request(
        url,
        headers={
            "User-Agent": "documind-svelte-crawler/1.0 (+https://svelte.dev)",
            "Accept": "text/html,application/xhtml+xml",
        },
    )
    with urlopen(request, timeout=timeout_seconds) as response:
        content = response.read()
    return content.decode("utf-8", errors="replace")

class LinkExtractor(HTMLParser):
    def __init__(self) -> None:
        super().__init__()
        self.links: list[str] = []

    def handle_starttag(self, tag: str, attrs: list[tuple[str, str | None]]) -> None:
        if tag != "a":
            return
        for key, value in attrs:
            if key == "href" and value:
                self.links.append(value)
                return

class TextExtractor(HTMLParser):
    SKIP_TAGS = {"script", "style", "noscript", "svg"}
    BLOCK_TAGS = {
        "article",
        "aside",
        "blockquote",
        "br",
        "div",
        "h1",
        "h2",
        "h3",
        "h4",
        "h5",
        "h6",
        "header",
        "li",
        "main",
        "nav",
        "ol",
        "p",
        "pre",
        "section",
        "table",
        "tr",
        "ul",
    }

    def __init__(self) -> None:
        super().__init__()
        self._parts: list[str] = []
        self._skip_depth = 0
        self._list_depth = 0
        self._heading_prefix: str | None = None

    def _push_break(self) -> None:
        if not self._parts:
            return
        if not self._parts[-1].endswith("\n"):
            self._parts.append("\n")

    def handle_starttag(self, tag: str, attrs: list[tuple[str, str | None]]) -> None:
        if tag in self.SKIP_TAGS:
            self._skip_depth += 1
            return
        if self._skip_depth > 0:
            return
        if tag in {"h1", "h2", "h3", "h4", "h5", "h6"}:
            self._push_break()
            level = int(tag[1])
            self._heading_prefix = "#" * level + " "
        if tag == "li":
            self._push_break()
            self._parts.append("- ")
        if tag in {"ul", "ol"}:
            self._list_depth += 1
            self._push_break()
        if tag in self.BLOCK_TAGS:
            self._push_break()

    def handle_endtag(self, tag: str) -> None:
        if tag in self.SKIP_TAGS and self._skip_depth > 0:
            self._skip_depth -= 1
            return
        if self._skip_depth > 0:
            return
        if tag in {"ul", "ol"} and self._list_depth > 0:
            self._list_depth -= 1
        if tag in self.BLOCK_TAGS:
            self._push_break()
        if tag in {"h1", "h2", "h3", "h4", "h5", "h6"}:
            self._heading_prefix = None

    def handle_data(self, data: str) -> None:
        if self._skip_depth > 0:
            return
        text = unescape(data).strip()
        if not text:
            return
        if self._heading_prefix:
            self._parts.append(self._heading_prefix)
            self._heading_prefix = None
        self._parts.append(text)
        self._parts.append(" ")

    def as_text(self) -> str:
        text = "".join(self._parts)
        text = re.sub(r"[ \t]+\n", "\n", text)
        text = re.sub(r"\n{3,}", "\n\n", text)
        text = re.sub(r"[ \t]{2,}", " ", text)
        return text.strip()

def extract_title(html: str) -> str:
    match = re.search(r"<title>(.*?)</title>", html, flags=re.IGNORECASE | re.DOTALL)
    if not match:
        return ""
    return unescape(match.group(1)).strip()

def extract_links(html: str, page_url: str) -> list[str]:
    parser = LinkExtractor()
    parser.feed(html)
    deduped: list[str] = []
    seen: set[str] = set()
    for raw in parser.links:
        normalized = normalize_url(raw, page_url)
        if normalized and normalized not in seen:
            deduped.append(normalized)
            seen.add(normalized)
    return deduped

def extract_text(html: str) -> str:
    parser = TextExtractor()
    parser.feed(html)
    return parser.as_text()

def filename_for_url(index: int, url: str) -> str:
    path = urlparse(url).path
    rel = path[len(ALLOWED_PREFIX) :] if path.startswith(ALLOWED_PREFIX) else path.strip("/")
    rel = rel.strip("/") or "index"
    rel = rel.replace("/", "__")
    rel = re.sub(r"[^a-zA-Z0-9._-]+", "-", rel)
    return f"{index:03d}_{rel}.md"

@dataclass
class PageRecord:
    url: str
    depth: int
    title: str
    file: str
    words: int
    link_count: int

def crawl(
    *,
    seed_url: str,
    out_dir: Path,
    max_depth: int,
    max_pages: int,
    timeout_seconds: int,
    delay_seconds: float,
) -> dict:
    normalized_seed = normalize_url(seed_url)
    if not normalized_seed:
        raise ValueError(f"Seed URL is outside allowed scope: {seed_url}")

    pages_dir = out_dir / "pages"
    pages_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)

    queue: deque[tuple[str, int]] = deque([(normalized_seed, 0)])
    queued: set[str] = {normalized_seed}
    visited: set[str] = set()
    page_records: list[PageRecord] = []
    failures: list[dict[str, str]] = []

    while queue and len(page_records) < max_pages:
        url, depth = queue.popleft()
        if url in visited:
            continue
        visited.add(url)

        try:
            html = fetch_html(url, timeout_seconds=timeout_seconds)
        except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001
            failures.append({"url": url, "error": str(exc)})
            continue

        title = extract_title(html)
        text = extract_text(html)
        links = extract_links(html, url)

        file_name = filename_for_url(len(page_records) + 1, url)
        file_path = pages_dir / file_name
        fetched_at = datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()
        rendered_title = title or url
        payload = (
            f"# {rendered_title}\n\n"
            f"Source: {url}\n"
            f"Fetched: {fetched_at}\n\n"
            f"{text}\n"
        )
        file_path.write_text(payload, encoding="utf-8")

        page_records.append(
            PageRecord(
                url=url,
                depth=depth,
                title=rendered_title,
                file=str(file_path),
                words=len(text.split()),
                link_count=len(links),
            )
        )

        if depth < max_depth:
            for link in links:
                if link not in visited and link not in queued:
                    queue.append((link, depth + 1))
                    queued.add(link)

        if delay_seconds > 0:
            time.sleep(delay_seconds)

    manifest = {
        "seed_url": normalized_seed,
        "allowed_scope": "https://svelte.dev/docs/svelte/*",
        "max_depth": max_depth,
        "max_pages": max_pages,
        "crawled_count": len(page_records),
        "failure_count": len(failures),
        "pages": [page.__dict__ for page in page_records],
        "failures": failures,
    }
    (out_dir / "manifest.json").write_text(json.dumps(manifest, indent=2), encoding="utf-8")
    return manifest

def parse_args() -> argparse.Namespace:
    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description="Crawl Svelte docs and export cleaned markdown files.")
    parser.add_argument("--seed-url", required=True)
    parser.add_argument("--out-dir", default=".documind/svelte_docs")
    parser.add_argument("--max-depth", type=int, default=2)
    parser.add_argument("--max-pages", type=int, default=60)
    parser.add_argument("--timeout-seconds", type=int, default=20)
    parser.add_argument("--delay-seconds", type=float, default=0.1)
    return parser.parse_args()

def main() -> int:
    args = parse_args()
    out_dir = Path(args.out_dir).resolve()
    manifest = crawl(
        seed_url=args.seed_url,
        out_dir=out_dir,
        max_depth=max(0, args.max_depth),
        max_pages=max(1, args.max_pages),
        timeout_seconds=max(5, args.timeout_seconds),
        delay_seconds=max(0.0, args.delay_seconds),
    )
    print(json.dumps(manifest, indent=2))
    return 0

if __name__ == "__main__":
    raise SystemExit(main())

#### ASSISTANT 33 (`phase: final_answer`)
```text
You’re right, and your script proves the main gap: **subpage discovery quality**, not ingestion.

The biggest issue in current backend crawler is scope filtering in [`resources.py`](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/resources.py:46).  
It uses the full seed path as the allowed prefix, so a seed like `/docs/svelte/overview` can exclude sibling docs pages.

### What I’d change (brainstormed design)

1. Fix crawl scope detection first.
- Infer `docs_root` from seed URL (example: `/docs/svelte/overview` -> `/docs/svelte/`).
- Let user override it in UI with “Scope path (optional)”.
- Add mode toggle: `Strict docs scope` (recommended) vs `Whole domain`.

2. Use multi-source link discovery, not just page anchors.
- Source A: `robots.txt` + sitemap index + sitemap URLs.
- Source B: nav/sidebar/TOC links from HTML.
- Source C: in-content anchor links.
- Source D: next/prev pagination links.
- Fallback: headless render (Playwright) only when static HTML yields too few links.

3. Rank and filter links before showing them.
- Keep same host, same scope path, drop binaries/assets/logout/etc.
- Canonicalize and dedupe (`canonical`, normalized URL, strip fragments/query noise).
- Score “doc-likeness” (URL pattern + page title/content length), show score in UI.

4. Make crawl a job-based workflow.
- Button 1: `Discover subpages`.
- Show live progress: discovered, queued, processed, failed.
- Show list with checkbox + “Select all high confidence”.
- Button 2: `Extract + Ingest selected`.

5. Improve multi-content crawling.
- Accept multiple seed URLs in one run.
- Merge all discovered links into one deduped queue.
- Per-domain concurrency + rate limit.
- Content hash per URL to skip unchanged pages on recrawl.

### Why your script worked
It hard-coded a clean scope (`/docs/svelte/`) and did BFS with depth/page limits.  
That pattern is solid. We should generalize it with dynamic scope inference + sitemap/nav extraction + job UI.

### Practical rollout
1. Phase 1: scope inference + sitemap/nav discovery + better filtering.  
2. Phase 2: crawl job progress UI + review/selection before ingest.  
3. Phase 3: multi-seed + incremental recrawl by content hash.

If you want, I can implement Phase 1 directly next in this codebase.
```

3. Same command outside sandbox succeeds immediately and returns your 8 instances (I reproduced that exact behavior with elevated execution).

4. Secondary issue in sandboxed agents: default context file path is home-based (`~/.documind/contexts.json`), which is not writable in this sandbox.  
Config source: [config.py:18](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/mcp_server/config.py:18)

Use this when running through agents:
```bash

Applied fix in code with 3 concrete changes:

2. Safe context-store path resolution with automatic `/tmp` fallback when `~/.documind` is not writable in [config.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/mcp_server/config.py:19).
3. Guarded context persistence so `context-set`/`init` returns structured error instead of crashing when store writes fail in [service.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/mcp_server/service.py:256).

How it works under the hood:

1. `dcli ... instances` reaches `DocuMindMCPService.list_instances()`, and any `httpx.ConnectError` is now classified.
2. If error text includes `operation not permitted`, response becomes:
   - `meta.error = "network_blocked"`
   - `meta.reason = "network_permission_denied"`
   - `meta.api_url` includes the target URL
   - actionable text explains sandbox/network restriction.
3. `load_settings()` now resolves context store path in this order:
   - `DOCUMIND_CONTEXT_STORE_PATH` (if set)
   - `~/.documind/contexts.json` (if writable)
   - `/tmp/documind/contexts.json` fallback.
4. `set_active_context()` wraps `_context_store.set(...)`; if write fails, it returns `reason: context_store_unwritable` instead of raising.

Tests added/updated:

1. [test_mcp_search_tool.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/tests/test_mcp_search_tool.py:400) for `network_blocked` and unwritable context store behavior.
2. [test_config.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/tests/test_config.py:1) for context-store path fallback logic.
3. Verified with: `uv run python -m unittest discover -s tests` (73 tests, all passing).

Important limitation: this does not bypass sandbox network policy; it makes failures explicit and prevents context-write crashes.  
To use this in your global `dcli`, reinstall the CLI package so pipx picks up these changes: `pipx reinstall documind-cli`.

1. **Prompt (Container / C4 style, best for updated architecture)**
```text
Create an updated architecture diagram for the "DocuMind" system using C4 Container style.

Context:
- Users:
  - Web User (browser)
  - Terminal User (DCLI)
  - AI Agent User (via MCP client)
- Client layer:
  - Next.js Frontend (dashboard + chat)
  - DCLI (documind_cli)
  - MCP Server (tool surface: search_docs, ask_docs, ingest_text, context tools)
- Application layer:
  - FastAPI Backend
  - Routers: instances, knowledge-bases, resources, query/search, memory, observability, health
  - Services: ingestion, retrieval, routing, agent, observability
- Data layer:
  - SQLite control-plane DB (instances, KBs, resources, query logs)
  - Actian VectorAI DB (vector collections/chunks)
  - Local context store file for CLI/MCP active context
- External:
  - Embedding provider
  - LLM provider

Required flows to visualize:
1) Ingest flow: frontend/CLI/MCP -> /resources -> parsing/chunking/embedding -> VectorAI upsert + SQLite metadata write
2) Search/Ask flow: frontend/CLI/MCP -> /search or /query (instance_id + namespace_id) -> retrieval -> vector search -> grounded response with sources
3) Fallback flow: primary /search/instance or /query/instance -> advanced hybrid fallback (/search/advanced, /query/advanced)
4) Context flow: context-set/context-show/contexts/context-delete for CLI + MCP

Diagram requirements:
- Left-to-right layout
- Clear trust boundaries: Client, Application, Data, External
- Label protocols (HTTP/JSON, MCP tool calls)
- Add a small legend
- Output in Mermaid code only (flowchart LR), no explanation
```

- Your app resolves `kb["collection_name"]` and searches it directly in [query.py:163](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/query.py:163) and [retrieval.py:212](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/services/retrieval.py:212), which calls [vectordb.py:67](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/vectordb.py:67).

  - `collections.list()` contains it
  - `collections.exists()` was `False`
  - `points.search()` returned the same `CollectionNotFoundError 404`

#### ASSISTANT 27 (`phase: final_answer`)
```text
You were right, it was breaking in backend LLM handling.

**Root cause**
- OpenAI call was failing, and code silently swallowed the exception, then returned local fallback text that looked like raw retrieved chunks.
- I reproduced this directly: backend had key loaded, but OpenAI call errored (`APIConnectionError` in this environment).
- There was also a client-init compatibility issue in the venv path (`proxies` arg) that I fixed by using an explicit `httpx.Client`.

**What I changed**
- Added explicit upstream LLM error type and configurable fallback behavior in [agent.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/services/agent.py#L9).
- Added `LLM_FALLBACK_ON_ERROR` config (default `false`) in [config.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/config.py#L35).
- Query routes now convert upstream LLM failures to HTTP `502` instead of silently returning raw-context fallback in [query.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/app/routers/query.py#L80).
- Added tests for this behavior in:
  - [test_agent_service.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/tests/test_agent_service.py#L1)
  - [test_query_router.py](/Users/mdkaifansari04/code/projects/vector-ai/documind/backend/tests/test_query_router.py#L222)

**Verification**
- Ran:
  - `.venv/bin/python -m unittest tests.test_agent_service tests.test_query_router tests.test_mcp_search_tool -v`
- Result: all passing (29 tests).

**What to do now**
1. Restart backend so new behavior is active.
2. Run your ask flow again.
3. If OpenAI is unreachable, you’ll now get a clear `502` error instead of misleading raw fallback output.
4. If you want old fallback behavior, set `LLM_FALLBACK_ON_ERROR=true` in `documind/backend/.env`.

I did not touch your existing frontend-modified files.
```
